The three finalists received US$450,000 to further mature the mission proposal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In December 2001, <i>Kepler</i> and <i>Dawn</i> were selected for flight by NASA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2001_105-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2001-105">[105]</a></sup> At this time only 80 exoplanets had been detected, and that was part of the mission of <i>Kepler</i>, to look for more exoplanets, especially Earth-sized.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2001_105-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2001-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> Both <i>Kepler</i> and <i>Dawn</i> were initially projected for launch in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated3_102-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated3-102">[102]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Discovery Program fell on hard-times after this, with several mission experiencing cost overruns, and the CONTOUR mission experiencing an engine failure in orbit. Although both <i>Dawn</i> and <i>Kepler</i> would become widely praised success stories, they missed their somewhat ambitious 2006 launch target, launching in 2007 and 2009 respectively. <i>Kepler</i> would go on to receive a mission extensions, and <i>Dawn</i> likewise successfully orbited both Vesta and Ceres. Nevertheless, the next selection would take longer than previous as the program selection of new missions slowed down. As the successes of the new missions enhanced the image of the Discovery Program, the difficulties began to fade from the limelight. Also, the number of active missions in development or active began to increase as the program ramped up.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Discovery_11">Discovery 11</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discovery_Program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Discovery 11">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The announcement of opportunity for this Discovery mission was released in April 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> There were three finalists for this Discovery selection including GRAIL (the eventual winner), OSIRIS, and VESPER.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-google1_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-google1-108">[108]</a></sup> OSIRIS was very similar to the later <a href="/wiki/OSIRIS-REx" title="OSIRIS-REx">OSIRIS-REx</a> mission, an asteroid sample return mission to <a href="/wiki/101955_Bennu" title="101955 Bennu">101955 Bennu</a>, and Vesper, a Venus orbiter mission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-google1_108-1"><a href="#cite_note-google1-108">[108]</a></sup> A previous proposal of Vesper had also been a finalist in the 1998 round of selection.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-google1_108-2"><a href="#cite_note-google1-108">[108]</a></sup> The three finalists were announced in October 2006 and awarded US$1.2 million to further develop their proposals for the final round.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2006_109-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2006-109">[109]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2007 NASA selected the <b><a href="/wiki/GRAIL" title="GRAIL">GRAIL</a></b> mission as the next Discovery mission, with a goal of mapping Lunar gravity and a 2011 launch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbcnews1_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-nbcnews1-110">[110]</a></sup> There were 23 other proposals that were also under consideration.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbcnews1_110-1"><a href="#cite_note-nbcnews1-110">[110]</a></sup> The mission had budget of US$375 million (then-year dollars) which included construction and also the launch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbcnews1_110-2"><a href="#cite_note-nbcnews1-110">[110]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Discovery_12">Discovery 12</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discovery_Program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Discovery 12">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:TSSM-TandEM-Lander.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="380" data-file-width="349" decoding="async" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/TSSM-TandEM-Lander.jpg/220px-TSSM-TandEM-Lander.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/TSSM-TandEM-Lander.jpg/330px-TSSM-TandEM-Lander.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/70/TSSM-TandEM-Lander.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:TSSM-TandEM-Lander.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Artist\'s impression of proposed TiME lake lander for Saturn\'s moon Titan</div></div></div>\n<p>This was an especially tough selection: coming on the heels of a successful Mars rover landing and the termination of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mars_Scout_program" title="Mars Scout program">Mars Scout program</a> (parent program of Phoenix and MAVEN), it meant that the proposals to the very popular red-planet competed with more obscure destinations. On the other hand, <a href="/wiki/Titan_(moon)" title="Titan (moon)">Titan</a> had just been landed on by <i>Huygens</i> and Comets were getting the full-treatment by the flagship-class ESA <i>Rosetta</i> mission.\n</p><p>28 proposals were received in 2010; according to the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>, 3 were for the Moon, 4 for Mars, 7 for Venus, 1 Jupiter, 1 to a Jupiter Trojan, 2 to Saturn, 7 to asteroids, and 3 to Comets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Out of the 28, three finalists received US$3 million in May 2011 to develop a detailed concept study:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/InSight" title="InSight">InSight</a></i>, a Mars lander.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Titan_Mare_Explorer" title="Titan Mare Explorer">Titan Mare Explorer</a> (TiME) spacecraft for landing in, and floating on, a large methane-ethane sea on <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">Saturn</a>\'s moon <a href="/wiki/Titan_(moon)" title="Titan (moon)">Titan</a>. A Titan moon "lake" lander was previously considered <a href="/wiki/Titan_Saturn_System_Mission" title="Titan Saturn System Mission">Titan Saturn System Mission</a> and other concepts, but have lost out to other missions which have themselves been cancelled.</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Comet_Hopper" title="Comet Hopper">Comet Hopper</a> (CHopper) study cometary evolution by landing on a comet multiple times and observing its changes as it interacts with the Sun.</li></ul>\n<p>In August 2012, <b>InSight</b> was selected for development and launch.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washington_114-0"><a href="#cite_note-washington-114">[114]</a></sup> The mission launched in May 2018 and successfully landed on Mars on November 26, 2018.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Discovery_13_and_14">Discovery 13 and 14</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discovery_Program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Discovery 13 and 14">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NASA_NEXT_Ion_thruster.712983main_NEXT_LDT_Thrusterhi-res_full.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4096" data-file-width="5461" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/NASA_NEXT_Ion_thruster.712983main_NEXT_LDT_Thrusterhi-res_full.jpg/220px-NASA_NEXT_Ion_thruster.712983main_NEXT_LDT_Thrusterhi-res_full.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/NASA_NEXT_Ion_thruster.712983main_NEXT_LDT_Thrusterhi-res_full.jpg/330px-NASA_NEXT_Ion_thruster.712983main_NEXT_LDT_Thrusterhi-res_full.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/NASA_NEXT_Ion_thruster.712983main_NEXT_LDT_Thrusterhi-res_full.jpg/440px-NASA_NEXT_Ion_thruster.712983main_NEXT_LDT_Thrusterhi-res_full.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:NASA_NEXT_Ion_thruster.712983main_NEXT_LDT_Thrusterhi-res_full.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>NASA made ion thruster technology available for proposals for the thirteenth Discovery Program mission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fp_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-fp-115">[115]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Selection_of_Discovery_Mission_13_and_14" title="Selection of Discovery Mission 13 and 14">Selection of Discovery Mission 13 and 14</a></div>\n<p>In February 2014, NASA released a Discovery Program \'Draft Announcement of Opportunity\' for launch readiness date of December 31, 2021.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup> On 30 September 2015, NASA selected five mission concepts as finalists,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-selection_1st_round_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-selection_1st_round-118">[118]</a></sup> each received $3 million for one-year of further study and concept refinement.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-laser2015_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-laser2015-119">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DAVINCI_(spacecraft)" title="DAVINCI (spacecraft)">Deep Atmosphere Venus Investigation of Noble gases, Chemistry, and Imaging</a> (DAVINCI)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/VERITAS_(spacecraft)" title="VERITAS (spacecraft)">Venus Emissivity, Radio Science, InSAR Topography and Spectroscopy</a> (VERITAS)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Near-Earth_Object_Camera" title="Near-Earth Object Camera">Near-Earth Object Camera</a> (NEOCam)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Lucy_(spacecraft)" title="Lucy (spacecraft)"><i>Lucy</i></a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Psyche_(spacecraft)" title="Psyche (spacecraft)"><i>Psyche</i></a></li></ul>\n<p>On January 4, 2017, <i><b><a href="/wiki/Lucy_(spacecraft)" title="Lucy (spacecraft)">Lucy</a></b></i> and <i><b><a href="/wiki/Psyche_(spacecraft)" title="Psyche (spacecraft)">Psyche</a></b></i> were selected for the 13th and 14th Discovery missions, respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasataps_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-nasataps-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasaselectslucypsyche_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-nasaselectslucypsyche-121">[121]</a></sup> <i>Lucy</i> will flyby five <a href="/wiki/Jupiter_trojan" title="Jupiter trojan">Jupiter trojans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asteroid" title="Asteroid">asteroids</a> which share Jupiter\'s <a href="/wiki/Orbit" title="Orbit">orbit</a> around the <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a>, orbiting either ahead of or behind the planet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20170106_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20170106-122">[122]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nasaselectslucypsyche_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-nasaselectslucypsyche-121">[121]</a></sup> <i>Psyche</i> will explore the origin of <a href="/wiki/Planetary_core" title="Planetary core">planetary cores</a> by orbiting and studying the metallic asteroid <a href="/wiki/16_Psyche" title="16 Psyche">16 Psyche</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20170106_122-1"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20170106-122">[122]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Discovery_15_and_16">Discovery 15 and 16</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discovery_Program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Discovery 15 and 16">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Proposal submissions for Discovery 15 and 16 missions will begin on February 28, 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-A_of_Opp_2019_123-0"><a href="#cite_note-A_of_Opp_2019-123">[123]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Summary">Summary</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discovery_Program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Summary">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Discovery has visited asteroids, comets, Mars, Mercury, and the Moon. There were two sample return missions, one for comet dust, another for solar wind, and that also detected <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Interstellar_dust" title="Interstellar dust">interstellar dust</a>, and one observatory focused on finding exoplanets.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Artists.27_impressions"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Artists\'_impressions">Artists\' impressions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Discovery_Program&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Artists\' impressions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="wikitable" style="margin: 1em auto 1em auto; width:90%">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="6">Discovery Program\n</th></tr>\n<tr style="background:white;">\n<td><div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Near_Shoemaker.jpg"><img alt="Near Shoemaker.jpg"
